Central Bank Inspection Report 141

Report on the 249th Inspection of the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Convertible Notes. In accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, the Council is responsible for inspecting the number of convertible notes issued by the Bank and the reserve funds. The 249th inspection was conducted at the Bank's Issuance Bureau on September 21, 24th year of the Republic of China. The inspection results are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 115,118,678 silver dollars, including 107,210,608 silver dollars and 7,908,070 subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of convertible note reserves is 115,118,678 silver dollars, including 88,300,8678 silver dollars in cash reserves. The cash reserves are deposited in the Bank's Issuance Treasury at 81,175,8067 yuan, in the Issuance Sub-bureau at 570,000 yuan, in various branches at 1,2534,781 yuan, and in counterpart banks at 3445,830 yuan. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 26,810,000 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 373,324.7 yuan. The total amount of customs gold convertible note reserves is 373,324.7 yuan. The reserve includes 7,351 taels, 9 mace, and 5 fen of standard gold, which is equivalent to 373,324.7 yuan of customs gold at a fixed price of 50779. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve shall be at least 60%, and the remainder shall be guaranteed with legal guarantee products. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the law. This is specially reported. September 23, 24th year of the Republic of China, Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank Ji Fuzi, Supervisors Xie Mengjun Beisongsun, Qin Runxiang, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilu.

The Liquidator of American-Oriental Banking Corporation is Commendable; Small Amounts are Paid in Full; Small Deposits are Equivalent to Approximately 50 Shanghai Dollars per Household; Reducing Liquidation Expenses is Actually Beneficial to Depositors 142

A few days ago, Mr. He Fu, the liquidator of the American-Oriental Banking Corporation, requested Mr. Hillmick, the Chief Judge of the United States Court for China, to approve the full payment of small amounts deposited in the bank, totaling approximately 42,000 yuan for 3,273 households. The presentation stated that the bank has now collected 625,000 yuan in cash. Before the liquidation is completed, the bank should have more funds than it currently has to distribute to depositors and creditors. There are 8,226 debtor accounts in total. The 3,273 accounts that are now proposed to be paid represent approximately 40% of the total. These deposits are all small amounts. Regardless of whether they are deposited in Shanghai dollars, Tianjin dollars, US dollars, Japanese yen, British pounds, Hong Kong dollars, French francs, or legal tender, they are equivalent to approximately 50 Shanghai dollars. If these small accounts can be fully paid, the liquidation work and expenses can be greatly reduced, and their total amount is not very large. As for the depositors and creditors who are not fully paid, the benefits of saving liquidation expenses are sufficient to offset the additional funds received by small households. Mr. He Fu's presentation was approved by Mr. Hillmick on Wednesday. The bank is now preparing to open for payment before October 1st. As for deposit interest, it is limited to those that have been settled into the account books. Those after the settlement date will not be paid. All depositors who owe debts to the bank that have not been cleared will not have their deposits returned.

Robbery and Murder Result in Two Deaths in Xiaohoujiazhai, Zhabei; One Victim Had Their Abdomen Cut Open and Intestines Spilled; the Other Had Three Knife Wounds to the Neck 143

Yesterday morning around 4:00 am, five or six robbers wearing blue-black short cloth jackets suddenly broke into the Wang Family Ancestral Hall in Xiaohoujiazhai, about two Huali north of Pengpu Town (commonly known as Miaotou) in Zhabei. Sha Jinkui, a 59-year-old man from Haimen who was in charge of guarding the ancestral hall, heard the noise and shouted for help. The robbers were furious and knocked Sha to the ground and stabbed him violently in the abdomen with a sharp blade, causing his abdomen to break open and his intestines to spill out. At the same time, Sha Jinkui's son-in-law, Liu Caiyi, and daughter, Liu Sha, also shouted and were stabbed three times in the neck by the robbers. They were lying in pools of blood. After committing the crime, the robbers, finding nothing of value in the room, snatched a wallet from the table in Liu Sha's bedroom and fled. By this time, someone had already reported to the Pengpu Town Police Station of the Xinzha Branch, and police were dispatched to the scene, capturing one robber, Wang Yongqing, 30 years old, from Tongzhou. A hatchet and a sharp knife were also found in the room. Police officer Gao Minglong rushed back to the police station and telephoned the Fire Joint Association to dispatch an ambulance to send the injured to the hospital. Liu Caiyi is currently in the Zhabei Jinshan Hospital, while Sha Jinkui's intestines were broken, and he was immediately sent to the Conscientious Hospital in the concession. According to the doctor, he had lost almost all of his blood and his injuries were extremely serious, and his life was in danger. The captured robber, along with the injured Liu Caiyi's wife, was taken to the police station. After a brief interrogation by patrol officer Xiang Zhaoxuan, the murder weapon and the hatchet were sent to the Xinzha Branch, which has been handed over to the detective team to arrest the remaining accomplices. According to Liu Sha, there were only two yuan in banknotes and a set of ten-yuan IOUs in the stolen wallet, as well as forty copper coins on the table, and nothing else.

Fire at the Xiechang Glass Factory's Celluloid Warehouse 144

The entire warehouse and three residential houses were destroyed; the total loss is estimated to be approximately 20,000 yuan.

The Xiechang Weiji Glass Factory, located at 163 Lane, Hujia Wood Bridge, Zhabei, was founded by Cantonese merchants Deng Zhongze and others, with Deng also serving as manager. The factory buildings were also built by themselves on a grand scale, specializing in the manufacture of glassware, which was widely sold. However, due to the sluggish market, business plummeted. Deng and the shareholders gathered to discuss and temporarily suspended the shipment of glassware from the factory, switching to the operation of celluloid toy equipment and other products on the market, but there was still no improvement. Therefore, they had no choice but to announce the shutdown of the factory. Unexpectedly, at around 12:00 noon yesterday, a fire suddenly broke out in the factory's celluloid raw material warehouse. It was found that most of the raw materials were highly flammable and explosive substances such as rosin. Once ignited, it spread immediately. In an instant, the entire warehouse became a sea of ​​fire, and it also affected three buildings at 7, 8, and 9, 189 Lane on the right. The general residents nearby were greatly alarmed and fled in confusion with the elderly and children. At that time, the fire was still fueling the flames and increasing unabated. Fortunately, the Zhabei fire brigades had received the alarm and rushed fire trucks to the scene, but due to the intense momentum and wide area, it was difficult to achieve immediate results. A gas smell caused people to vomit. The firefighters were afraid of further spread, so they all fought bravely to put out the fire and raised cloud ladders to pour water from above and below. After about two hours of continuous watering, the fire gradually went out, but the smoke had not completely dissipated, so the Hongzhen District fire truck was left on the scene to continue to extinguish it. As a result, the factory and the three residences at 7, 8, and 9, 189 Lane, were completely destroyed, with a total loss estimated at approximately 20,000 yuan. Only the Xiechang Factory had fire insurance of 10,000 yuan. The cause of the fire has not been ascertained. The police station in charge has summoned Deng Zhuang, the bookkeeper of the Xiechang Glass Factory, for questioning and awaits verification.

Couple Commits Suicide Due to Poverty; Wife Dies, Husband is in Danger 145

Shandong people Shi Yuxi and his wife Wang Xushi, both 31 years old, previously lived at 8 Xinqiao Road, Nanshi, where they worked as factory workers to make a living. On the 20th of this month, the couple moved into the kitchen shed in the extra rooms of Liu Ni, a woman from Yancheng (40 years old), at 4 Yuanfuli, Belle Road, French Concession, with a monthly rent of three dollars. They only had one dollar saved when they moved in, and two dollars were still unpaid. The Wang couple had been unemployed for a long time, and their life gradually became difficult. Unable to find a way to make a living and struggle, the couple had the idea of ​​committing suicide together. On the night of the 24th, they found poison, swallowed it, and went to bed together, waiting for death to come. On the morning of the next day (25th) at 7:00 am, a friend of Wang went to Wang's residence and knocked on the door. When there was no response, he tried to open the door and went inside to check. He saw the Wang couple sleeping on the bed, already dying, and was shocked. He immediately informed the second landlord, Liu Ni, and reported to the French police, who sent detectives to investigate. Wang Yuxi and Wang Xushi, husband and wife, were sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. Wang Xushi died at 12:30 pm that night due to ineffective treatment. The hospital notified the police to transport the body to the Funeral Parlor of the Conscientious Hospital for an autopsy. Wang Chengzhai (22 years old, living in the Second Civilian Residence on Xietu Road, also a small worker), the nephew of the deceased, was summoned to the case. Yesterday, it was reported to the Special Second Court, and Prosecutor Wang Ren came to the station to confirm that Wang Xushi had indeed died from taking poison before death. The body was allowed to be taken by the nephew of the deceased, Wang Chengzhai, for burial. At the same time, Wang Yuxi, the husband who took poison, is still being treated in Shici Hospital. It is reported that the situation is very critical. Whether he can escape the danger depends on whether he can pass the dangerous period.

No Suspicion of Hua Azeng in the Nanchezhan Road Assassination Case; The Police Have Found Out the Facts; He Has Been Released on 3,000 Yuan Bail 146

At 11:45 am on the 20th of this month, an assassination suddenly occurred at the entrance of 14 Furunli, Nanshi Chezhan Road. The victim was Bao Xiangfan Shun, a tea house contractor at the Wing On Company's Tiantianyuan Building. Later, according to Xiang's wife, Ms. Chen, she reported to the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Investigation Department that her husband had said before his death that the murderer was Hua Azeng, the general contractor of the Yong An Tea House, a Ningbo native. Detective team leader Gao Wansheng and others, together with Wang Shusen, a detective from the Laozha Police Station, arrested Hua at 24 Guangxi Road and sent him to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning, the police transferred Hua back to the Criminal Court of the Special First Court. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stated that the case was originally scheduled to be heard on Saturday. However, as instructed by the court, if the police found that Hua had no criminal suspicion, the case should be advanced. Now, police detectives first went to Shanghai Hospital to investigate. Dr. Chen of Shanghai Hospital received them and said that he and the nurses had not heard the deceased mention that the murderer was Hua Azeng. Later, the detectives also found out that Hua had stayed at his concubine Hua Ma's house at 1,000 Tongpu Road on the night of the 19th until 11:00 am the next morning, and then met with Yu Yongkang and more than a dozen other people to talk. At 2:00 pm, he went to Wing On Company to talk with Wang Yingzhou and others. At 4:00 pm, he went to his wife Hua Zhu's place at 24 Guangxi Road. The police detectives interviewed Yu Yongkang and others one by one, and their statements were consistent. Therefore, it is requested that the motion to transfer from the Public Security Bureau be decided that it is not necessary to transfer it. Then Wang Tanmu submitted a report on the investigation process. The court then ordered that the debate on the transfer issue begin. After the police lawyer Wang and Hua's lawyers Xue Dubi and Yu Xiangqin debated each other, Judge Qian Hongye ruled that Hua Azeng should be released on 3,000 yuan bail and be instructed to report to the Public Security Bureau himself.

Using Eating Vegetarian Food Together as a Pretext; Staying in a Convent and Refusing to Leave: Wu Jinsheng of the Lu Family Convent Files a Lawsuit; Zhou Jiantang Also States His Reasons 147

Wu Jinsheng, a Hangzhou native residing at No. 20, Lane inside the Sming Hospital entrance, Avenue Edward VII, French Concession, at the Lu Family Convent, recently engaged a lawyer to submit a petition to the criminal court of the Special Court, accusing Zhou Jiantang, a Ningbo native who also resides there, and Zhou's brother-in-law, Ye Dingyi, of obstructing freedom. It is alleged that the defendants have intruded into the residence without reason, staying and refusing to leave, causing disturbances. It is stated that Wu Dakun, the father of the plaintiff, was a vegetarian Buddhist. He bought land and built a house on Avenue Edward VII to house idols. After the grandfather's death, all property was transferred to the plaintiff for management. The defendants, using vegetarianism as a pretext, forcibly moved in and refused to leave, depriving the plaintiff of freedom. The plaintiff requests that the court investigate and punish them according to Articles 306, sections 1 and 2 of the Criminal Code. Based on the petition, the court summoned both parties yesterday for questioning. Judge Chen Pusheng opened the second criminal court for the trial. The plaintiff first testified as above. The defendant, Zhou Jiantang, testified that at the age of eighteen, he became a disciple of Yang Dakun, also known as Putian, and became a vegetarian Buddhist with the Dharma name Putai. In the seventh year of the Republic, he and his master Putian raised 1,000 yuan, bought a piece of land on Avenue Edward VII, spent 70 yuan, and built three bungalows. After the master's death, all the seals and yellow cloth bags used for promoting Dharma were handed over to me for management and safekeeping, and a seal with the inscription 'Putai at the Head' was also made (and presented to the court at the time of testimony). All property was entrusted to me for management, but the land deeds disappeared after the houses were built. Later, I learned that Wu Jinsheng had pawned them for 300 yuan at a Mr. Xu's place at No. 18, Yongye Lane, Weihai Road. Recently, Wu said that the land deed has been re-mortgaged for 1,000 yuan. According to the testimony of witness Qin Jiji, 47 years old, a Ningbo native, the deceased Master Putian, i.e. the plaintiff's grandfather, was in charge of the temple. After his death, his younger brother Zhou Jiantang succeeded him. The land was bought in the eighth year of the Republic for 70 yuan. The funds for building the house were raised jointly by Putian and Zhou Jiantang. After the houses were built, the land deeds were stolen, but Zhou Jiantang pays the annual land tax. According to the testimony of witness Pu Bai, 60 years old, a Suzhou native residing in Xiaobeimen, he calls Zhou Jiantang 'Grandpa'. He donated 50 yuan when the temple was built. He does not know the plaintiff. After reviewing the testimony, the court decided that the case required further investigation and adjourned the hearing to October 4th.

The Shanghai Times reports that Mr. Gorlt Hill, the American cookie king, arrived in Shanghai on Wednesday morning, intending to purchase two million pounds of dried eggs, and hoping to acquire several egg factories here, or obtain their management rights, within twelve days. Recently, due to the rising prices of eggs produced in the United States, it is now planning to buy two million pounds of dried eggs from China annually.

Premeditated Murder Case Awaits Sentencing 149

Dong Chenggui from Haimen and Lu Shouchang (also known as Si Quan), a local, used to work together as butchers at Tan Arong's pig slaughterhouse on Yuezhou Road. Tan's wife, Azhu, secretly became acquainted with Lu. After Tan's death, they openly cohabited as husband and wife. Dong knew the whole story and informed Tan's friends, Xiang Dongsheng from Baoshan and Shen A'er from Jiangyin. Everyone felt indignant about this matter and contributed money to hire soldier A'wu. Around 1:00 AM on the 22nd of September in the 18th year of the Republic, at an open space on Yuezhou Road, Zhaofeng Road, A'wu opened fire on Lu Shouchang, attempting to kill him, and then fled. Later, Dong Chenggui was arrested and sentenced to six years of penal servitude. He confessed that Xiang had provided 100 yuan beforehand, and that he and Shen had discussed the plan in a small hotel opened in Dongxin Bridge in the French Concession before carrying it out. On the 17th of this month at 7:00 PM, Inspector Yan Rongshi of the Detective Department of Avenue Foch, located in the Zhongxin Teahouse at No. 30, Beihai Road, Xinzha Road, apprehended Xiang and Shen. They were taken to the First Special District Court for questioning, where they denied the charges. It was ordered to postpone the hearing and bring Dong for identification. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi visited the Third Criminal Court for review. The representative of the Public Works Department, Zhishan, stated that, in the postponement, the two defendants were placed in a group of five other prisoners at the Detective Department for Dong to identify. Dong identified them correctly without error. Now, Dong is also present in court for questioning. A public prosecution was initiated against them for attempted murder under Article 271 of the Criminal Code. Lu Shouchang testified that he and the two defendants were all acquaintances in the same industry. Tan's wife, Azhu, had been living with him since her husband's death and there was no relationship before his death. At the time, he saw three people. Dong said, "The old man is here!" and immediately heard a gunshot. He ran away and escaped, suffering a slight bullet wound to his shoulder. Dong Chenggui claimed that he went with A'wu Wang Yougen at the time. A'wu fired the gun and the matter has nothing to do with the two defendants. He completely overturned everything he had testified in court before and at the Detective Department's identification. Xiang and Shen resolutely denied conspiracy and hired lawyers to defend them. Judge Jiang ordered that they be remanded in custody to await sentencing.

Repeated Kidnapping Cases: Notorious Bandits Under Interrogation. The Circumstances Are Serious and Still Under Investigation. The Bandits Are Remanded in Custody for Further Hearings 150

The notorious bandit Zhou Zhiliang, on the night of June 12th, 17th year of the Republic, along with Xue Xi'en and over thirty others, each armed with pistols and sharp blades, stormed into Zhang Zhanqing's house in the Yu Dong Six Jia Town, North Five Jia area of Nantong County, robbing property. When the owner resisted, it triggered the anger of the bandits, who killed Zhang Zhanqing's mother, Zhang Yangshi, and his brothers, Zhang Tianfu and Zhang Guangshun. Before fleeing, the bandits set fire to firewood and threw the corpses into the fire to destroy the evidence. They also shot and injured three members of the owner's family. The relevant authorities issued a warrant for their arrest. It is now known that Zhou Zhiliang, finding it difficult to stay in his hometown, fled to Shanghai. In November of last year, he gathered a gang to kidnap a certain person and demand a ransom. Then, on the morning of December 30th at around 7:00 AM, he gathered a gang at the end of Gordon Road and kidnapped Liu Shunde, the owner of the Lide Oil Factory in Xiaoshadu, demanding a ransom. Later, he kidnapped a Mr. Wu on Carter Road. The case was uncovered, and Zhang Weilin, Wu Yunbao and others who were suspected were arrested and brought to the local court. After several interrogations by Prosecutor Ouyang Shu, it was determined that Zhou Zhiliang and others were to be prosecuted for robbery, murder, and kidnapping for ransom. Briefly, Zhou Zhiliang acted together in robbery and intentionally committed murder, and injured more than two people, violating Article 1, Section 12 of the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Bandits. Zhang Weilin and Wu Yunbao repeatedly kidnapped people for ransom, and all violated Article 1, Section 1 of the aforementioned regulations. All should be sentenced according to Articles 9 and 42 of the Criminal Code. Zhou Zhiliang committed several crimes and should be sentenced according to Article 9 of the aforementioned and Article 69 and Article 70, Section 1 of the same law. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Tan Zhuohong specially opened the 11th courtroom for the trial. The defendant Zhang Weilin hired Lawyer Tao Ran to defend him in court. After the judge took the seat, he ordered that all the defendants be brought to the case. Zhou Zhiliang testified that he was 36 years old and from Tongzhou, and claimed that he was being framed. The judge said, "You committed a major case in Tongzhou, killing three people. The pistol is also yours, and thirteen pieces of original stolen clothing, trousers, and skirts were found in your house. Zhang Zhanqing's mother, Zhang Yangshi, was shot dead by you. Today, you still think of denying it in court. You should confess truthfully." He replied, "It's a wrongful accusation. My family has a 74-year-old mother, and a wife and children, a family of eight, all relying on me for a living. I request an investigation." Next, Zhang Weilin testified that he was 34 years old and from Tongzhou, earning a living by working. The judge asked, "In November of last year, you and your accomplices engaged in kidnapping." He replied, "There is no such thing." The judge asked, "On December 30th of last year, you went to kidnap Liu Shunde, the owner of Lide Oil Factory, for ransom." He replied, "It's a wrongful accusation." The judge asked, "How did you get arrested?" He replied, "A friend named Lu Guiqing borrowed money from me to smoke opium. I am against smoking and drinking, so I didn't lend it to him. He held a grudge and instigated false witnesses, accusing me of being a kidnapper. It's really a grave injustice, and I will die with my eyes not closed." Lai Yunbao testified that he was 44 years old, from Tongzhou, and made a living by pulling a rickshaw. Although he is from the same hometown as Zhou Zhiliang and Zhang Weilin, he does not know them. He used to work as a store clerk in Hongchang Sheng Fruit, responsible for delivering goods, for a total of 24 years. He has never committed a crime, and asks for investigation. The judge ruled, based on the testimony, that the circumstances of the case were serious and required further investigation. He scheduled a date to summon witnesses for further hearings. All defendants were remanded in custody pending further instructions.

Bloodshed Case on North Henan Road: The Issue of Opening the Safe Deposit Box. The Bank Has No Knowledge of the Items Inside the Box. The Signature on the Account Matches the Signature Card. 151

Regarding the news of the tragic death of the housewife and maid in the bloodshed case on North Henan Road, which was reported in this newspaper yesterday, involving the safe deposit box incident at the Shanghai Bank, the bank has sent a letter stating that there are discrepancies with the facts. The original letter is reproduced below to clarify the truth. The letter states: "To the Editor: We have read the news of the tragic death of the housewife and maid in the bloodshed case on North Henan Road in your newspaper, which is quite detailed. However, there are two points that do not conform to the facts. We hereby explain them as follows: (Point 1) '...However, the bank, in order to comply with banking practice, refused to disclose the contents of the safe deposit box...' It is the customer's responsibility to place items in the safe deposit box, and the bank has no right to interfere, nor does it have any knowledge of its contents. The so-called refusal to disclose the contents of the safe deposit box was probably due to the fact that when the Western detective came to the bank to inquire, there was no court order, nor could he point out the account number and correct account name. Our bank was unable to answer at that time due to this misunderstanding. (Point 2) '...The defendant also claimed that he had stolen the key to the safe deposit box of the Shanghai Bank ten days ago, and then secretly engraved a seal and went to the Shanghai Bank to open the box and obtain a lot of wealth...' When a safe deposit box is rented, the seal must be submitted to the bank for comparison when opening the box in the future. The procedure is strict and prudent, and there is no way to open the box with a fake seal. After reading the account number in your newspaper, our bank immediately checked the signature card left by the customer to see whether the box was opened with a seal or a signature. Since renting the box, the customer has always used a signature to open the box. On the 23rd of this month, when the customer came to open the box, they also used a signature, and this signature was verified by our bank to be consistent with the signature card, and there is a record of the entry into the vault. The so-called secret engraving of the seal, if the defendant was not delirious when giving testimony, it was a mistake in the record. Our bank, due to business relations, cannot but solemnly declare this."

Page 12

Yue Gengxin Talks About His Trip Investigating the Sugar Industry in the Dutch East Indies 152

Mr. Zhu Gengxin, a standing member of the Shanghai Sugar Industry Association and manager of Xinyi Company, after investigating the sugar industry in the Dutch East Indies since August 1st of this year, and taking the opportunity to visit various sugar factories and sugarcane areas in Guangzhou, has now been two months. Mr. Zhu conducted a detailed investigation into the sugar production in various places in the Dutch East Indies, and was warmly welcomed by local officials and businessmen in negotiating the development of domestic product production and sales. Mr. Zhu returned to Shanghai on the 24th aboard the Dutch steamship Zhimin Canada, intending to contribute his findings to the industry. The reporter interviewed Mr. Zhu at Xinyi Company and asked about his trip. He graciously made the following remarks.

The Decline of the Javanese Sugar Industry

Mr. Zhu began by saying that he has been engaged in the sugar industry in Shanghai for nearly twenty years, and his long-cherished wish is to promote the Chinese sugar industry, so it is necessary to go to Java, the most prosperous place of sugar production, for investigation. "This time, my impression of Java is particularly good. The place is rich in resources and densely populated, and its importance is second to none among the islands. Sugar is the main product, followed by coffee. I have been to Batavia, Surabaya, Samarang and other ports. The municipal facilities in various places are very complete. The Dutch Sugar Company sent specialists to guide me to visit various sugar factories and sugarcane areas one by one. The advancement of production technology, the scientific management of factories, and the perfection of transportation tools between factories and sugarcane fields can all be used as a mirror for our country's sugar industry. However, under the shroud of this global economic downturn, the Javanese sugar industry also shows signs of decline. There were originally more than 180 sugar factories there, but now there are only thirty. The economic sector has suffered greatly."

The Dutch East Indies Has Not Banned the Import of Domestic Goods

Mr. Zhu continued, "I took advantage of this opportunity to go to Java to investigate the sugar industry and discussed the sales of domestic goods in the Dutch East Indies. The reason why domestic goods cannot be sold there is mostly due to poor sales methods, such as the exported goods not matching the samples, losing the trust of overseas Chinese, and the lack of sound sales agencies to compete with foreign goods. When I was in Java, I met with the economic committee of the Dutch East Indies, Consul Song of Batavia, Consul Guo of Surabaya, and the chairman of the Chinese Chamber of Commerce, to discuss the issue of developing foreign trade. All parties are willing to do their best to assist in the sale of domestic goods in the Dutch East Indies. For the sake of developing domestic goods, the overseas Chinese in Batavia have proposed holding a domestic goods exhibition in Batavia, which will soon become a reality. I hope that the Chinese people will work together and cooperate with the overseas Chinese to open up a garden for the development of domestic goods. It is rumored that the Dutch East Indies government prohibits the import of domestic goods, which is not true. It is true that the Dutch East Indies prohibits the import of foreign goods, but most of what it prohibits are certain foreign goods, and purely Chinese products are not among the prohibited items, but there are considerable restrictions."

The Guangdong Sugar Industry is Very Developed

Mr. Zhu finally said, "Guangdong is the most prosperous place for sugar production in our country. I specially went to Guangzhou for investigation when I returned to Shanghai. I was cordially received by Feng Rui, the Director of the Agricultural and Forestry Bureau of Guangdong Province, and the Manager of the First Sugarcane Factory in Guangzhou District of the Provincial Government. I was taken to visit various sugar factories and benefited a lot. The factories are equipped with new-style machines that can be used to make sugar from raw materials and to refine sugar from raw sugar. The factory equipment, management, and the efforts of the staff can all be used as a reference for us. What is regrettable is that the transportation is not perfect, which has a great impact on sugar production. In Java, there are light railways all over between the manufacturing plant and the sugarcane area, and the transportation is very convenient. In Guangdong, all are transported by boat. Due to the inconvenience of transportation, the sugar juice of sugarcane is greatly reduced. If improvements can be made in this area, the sugar juice of sugarcane can be increased by six or seven percent, and in a few years, it should be able to meet the needs of the whole country. These sugar factories are all large in scale. It is said that several sugar factories will also appear in Shantou next spring."

Special Article

Opinions on the Issue of Increasing Capital (6) 157

(8) Application after the Concentration of Financial Power

As mentioned above, the progress of the financial system is seen in the concentration of power and the flexibility of turnover. In recent years, both the banking and money industries have their own joint reserve organizations. A few months ago, the money industry also abandoned its business of acting as an agent for banks to collect, disburse, and deposit bank reserves, transforming the abnormal downward distribution of reserves into a proper upward concentration. After the Central Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Third Bank increased their capital and changed their organizational structure, followed by the transfer of management of some issuing banks, the movement of concentrating financial power has roughly taken shape. However, regarding measures to promote the flexibility of turnover, although efforts have been made separately by allowing the Central Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Third Bank to provide financing and mortgages to the money industry, and by organizing the Industrial and Commercial Loan Committee to provide funds to general industrial and commercial enterprises, the trend is still to rely on the existing credit capital and the current lending system as a stopgap measure, failing to actively promote the establishment of modern credit capital and the grand scale of the financial industry. This is, of course, because the great disaster is imminent, and the situation is unstable, making it difficult to see long-term plans. However, in light of the principle that adversity builds a nation, future efforts should focus on using new credit capital to achieve the goal of flexible turnover, thereby creating an epoch-making progress in the financial industry.

Regarding the issuance of corporate bonds, Committee Member Chen Xiaodie once suggested using corporate bonds to exchange for financial public bonds. This may hinder the development of a long-term capital market for industry and commerce. After corporate bonds are exchanged for national bonds, what remains on the market will still be public bonds and treasury bills, and corporate bonds will not be included. In other words, the existing securities market will still be a financial securities market and will not be able to generate a long-term capital market for industry and commerce. Moreover, at a time when the state's finances are in deficit, the government must reserve a margin in the issuance of public bonds to cope with financial emergencies. Whether it can use more spare capacity for the exchange of corporate bonds is also questionable. We believe that the most important institutions for promoting corporate bonds are the underwriting agency and the trading market. Regarding the latter, the Chinese Securities Exchange can certainly assume its responsibility. Regarding the former, although the above article advocates that banks should vigorously promote underwriting as much as possible, the results will be slow, which is undeniable. To find a quick solution, we must open up new paths. The Central Trust Bureau is now ready. If the bureau can be used as the center to unite the financial industry and separately organize various syndicates for underwriting the issuance of various corporate bonds, the results will be faster. According to the underwriting business, which is originally a type of trust business, the Central Trust Bureau can naturally assume it. The most important thing in promoting any new movement is to establish a central force. If the Central Trust Bureau can lead the way, the financial industry will not find it difficult to follow and make it a success. This is better than the limited assistance provided by the government directly through the exchange of public bonds.

The main key to promoting bank acceptance bills and commercial acceptance bills is the rediscount of national banks. Only when national banks can provide general financial institutions with rediscount facilities can general financial institutions have nothing to fear and be able to provide strong financing to industrial and commercial enterprises by purchasing and discounting bills. The financing of national banks to general financial institutions, except when the international balance of payments is in deficit and cash must be used, is usually just a matter of transferring accounts. The reserves of ordinary banks are mostly concentrated in national banks, and the funds payable by Bank A are often the funds receivable by Bank B. The financing provided by the national bank to Bank A often goes directly into Bank B's deposit account in the national bank. Currently, the Central Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Third Bank have formed a tripartite alliance, and the trend of concentrating reserves in the three banks has been largely completed. With the cooperation of the three banks, it goes without saying that they can assume the task of rediscounting. If, in terms of issuance, we can follow the precedents of various countries in the East and West and appropriately incorporate bank acceptance bills and commercial acceptance bills as guarantee reserves, then the bills received by the three banks in the rediscounting business can be transformed into guarantee reserves to increase issuance. This will then provide a satisfactory solution to the demand for increasing payment capital. (To be continued)

Educational News

National Children's Relief: Measures for Disaster-Stricken Children 172

Implementation Period: October 10th to December 10th

The "National Children's Relief Measures for Disaster-Stricken Children" have been drafted by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee and submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval and issued to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces to follow. The measures are as follows:

1. These measures are specifically aimed at mobilizing children nationwide to assist in providing relief to children in disaster-stricken areas, mobilizing junior high and elementary school children nationwide to raise money and goods in the shortest possible time to provide relief to children in flood-affected areas.

2. Participants in the disaster relief effort will primarily consist of junior high and elementary school children (excluding kindergarten students), with educational administrative personnel and junior and elementary school faculty and staff responsible for guidance and supervision.

3. The implementation period for these measures will be two months, from October 10th, 1935, to December 10th, 1935.

4. The implementation of these measures will be divided into three steps:

Step 1: Fundraising

(1) The fundraising period will be one month, from October 10th, 1935, to November 10th, 1935. (2) For the fundraising procedures, the National Children's Year Implementation Committee will first submit these measures to the Ministry of Education for distribution to the education departments of various provinces, which will then instruct the relevant educational administrative organs in various counties and cities, and distribute them to the directly administered cities of the Executive Yuan, instructing their subordinate schools to comply. (3) The scope of fundraising items will be limited to cash and children's clothing, pants, hats, shoes, socks, quilts (old but clean items are also acceptable), etc. (4) After receiving these measures, local schools should immediately organize a disaster relief group for children in disaster-stricken areas, with the principal as the leader, and set up propaganda, fundraising, and safekeeping groups. Teachers should be appointed to serve as the leaders of each group, and older children (over ten years old) should be assigned to serve as members of each group. If the number of students in a school is too small to organize independently, they may jointly organize with nearby schools. (5) The duties of the group leader are as follows: 1. Organize the disaster relief group for children in disaster-stricken areas, appoint group leaders, and direct the work of each group. 2. Plan the steps for the group's progress. 3. Supervise each group to work hard. 4. Compile fundraising results and report to the relevant educational administrative organs. (7) The duties of the propaganda group are as follows: 1. Post slogans and paintings related to the disaster situation in disaster-stricken areas. 2. Draft the fundraising goals of the group and publish them in local newspapers or distribute leaflets. 3. Screen films about the floods (in consultation with local public education centers). 4. Describe the flood situation in various places. 5. Hold disaster relief performances. (7) The duties of the fundraising group are as follows: 1. Solicit donations from teachers, students, alumni, and other staff members of the school. 2. Solicit donations from the parents of students at the school. 3. Solicit donations from the neighbors of the students at the school. (8) The duties of the safekeeping group are as follows: 1. Keep the collected funds safe. 2. Keep the collected items safe. 3. Record fundraising results and report to the group leader. (9) In addition to soliciting donations from others for money and goods, each child (except for those who are truly impoverished) should donate the following amount of money: 1. Children in lower elementary school: save one copper coin per day on candy, totaling thirty coins per month. 2. Children in upper elementary school: save two copper coins per day on candy, totaling sixty coins per month. 3. Children in junior high school: save five copper coins per day on pocket money, totaling one hundred and fifty coins per month.

Step 2: Remittance

(1) Each school should prepare a detailed list of the money and goods collected and remit them to the relevant educational administrative organs in each county and city before November 15th, and make a detailed list of the money and goods raised by each child and the amount of money donated by each person, and post it at the school gate, and inform each child. (2) The relevant educational administrative organs in each county and city should prepare a detailed list of the money and goods collected by each school in the county and city and remit them to the relevant education departments before November 20th, and publish the detailed figures of the fundraising achievements of each school in the county in the newspaper for reference by each school. (3) The education departments and bureaus of each province and city should remit the collected money to the Central Relief Committee before November 30th, and report the list of goods to the Central Relief Committee. After the Central Relief Committee has determined the distribution, the education departments and bureaus of each province and city should send them directly to the nearby disaster-stricken areas, and compile the fundraising achievements of the entire province and city. The city should publish the detailed figures of the fundraising achievements of each school in the newspaper, and the province should publish the detailed figures of the fundraising achievements of each county and city in the newspaper, and distribute them to the relevant departments (schools for cities, counties for provinces), and report them to the Ministry of Education, and notify the National Children's Year Implementation Committee for verification.

Step 3: Distribution and Awards

(1) The Central Relief Committee, together with the Ministry of Education, the National Children's Year Implementation Committee, and the provincial education departments in the disaster-stricken areas, will properly distribute the collected money and goods before December 12th, taking into account the severity of the disaster in various places, and compile the fundraising achievements of children nationwide and publish them in newspapers. (2) The money and goods will be distributed to various relief agencies, and each agency will issue a receipt for the goods and give them to the disaster-stricken children. (3) With the consent of the Ministry of Education and the National Children's Year Implementation Committee, a portion of the money may be set aside to establish shelters for children in disaster-stricken areas and provide them with appropriate education and care. (4) Local children's year implementation committees should award honorary certificates to the schools and children with the best fundraising performance in their respective regions. The schools and children with the best fundraising performance in each province and city and nationwide will be awarded by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee.

5. When schools in various places raise money and goods for disaster relief, local educational administrative personnel and the hunting clothes year implementation committee should be responsible for supervision, guidance, and oversight.

6. If the school is located in a disaster-stricken area, the collected money and goods may be directly handed over to the local relief agency for distribution to the disaster-stricken children, while a list should be prepared and submitted to the relevant educational administrative organs.

7. If the county or city where the county and city educational administrative organs are located has disaster-stricken areas, all or part of the money and goods collected in the entire county or city may be directly handed over to the county and city relief agencies for distribution to the disaster-stricken children, while a list should be prepared and submitted to the relevant education departments.

8. If the province where the provincial education department is located has disaster-stricken areas, all or part of the money and goods collected in the entire province may be directly handed over to the provincial relief agencies for distribution to the disaster-stricken children, while a list should be prepared and submitted to the Central Relief Committee, the Ministry of Education, and the National Children's Year Implementation Committee.

9. If there are any errors in the handling of the funds by the agencies, the children's year implementation committees of each province, city, and county will report them. If the circumstances are serious, the person in charge will be dismissed and prosecuted according to law.

10. These measures will be implemented upon approval by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee. (Central News Agency, Nanjing, 26th) The National Children's Year Implementation Committee, based on the resolutions of the Fifth Congress, has drafted "National Children's Relief Measures for Disaster-Stricken Children," which have been submitted to the Ministry of Education for instruction to all junior high and elementary schools nationwide to follow. The implementation period will be from Double Tenth Day of this year to December 10th.

Little Men (5) (8) 186

— Original by American Ms. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

Mr. Bae saw the cow and heard the story. He didn't say much, obviously fearing that he would be unable to restrain himself under the sudden shock and would say too much. He just settled Lao Huanghua in her shed and asked the children to go back to their rooms and come out for dinner.

Such a short rest gave them an opportunity to think about this matter once, to guess what punishment they would receive, and to imagine where Dunn would be sent. He was in his own room, just whistling to himself, putting on an indifferent attitude; but as he waited for the decision of his fate, the desire to stay gradually grew stronger, as he recalled the comfort and good treatment he had received here, and the suffering and indifference he had encountered elsewhere. He knew they were trying to help him, and deep down he was grateful, but the rough life he had encountered had made him a cold, reckless, suspicious, and stubborn person. He hated any restrictions, even when he knew they were well-intentioned and it seemed he could really benefit from them, but he still resisted them, like an untamed beast. He was determined to return to that wandering life, bumping around the streets, as he had lived his entire life; the thought of that future made him tighten his thick black eyebrows, and he looked around the comfortable little room with a look of attachment. If Mr. Bae had seen this, his heart, even if it had been many times harder, would have been moved. These thoughts disappeared immediately when that good man came in and said in his inherent solemn tone:

"I've heard everything, Dunn. Although you've broken the rules for the second time, I'm going to give you another chance, to please Mrs. Bae."

Chunqiu (Spring and Autumn)

Tidbits 187

— (Liu Fangdi)

Time is like a runaway horse, and people are poisoned by its galloping, turning red faces into white hair.

No peace is comparable to the peace of conscience. The tranquility in this small space is like the harmony obtained by heaven and earth.

Don't waste a shallow cup of water, knowing that the traveler in the vast Gobi Desert travels thousands of miles and cannot find a sweet spring!

Although the moth buries its small life in the blazing flames, it is ultimately a heroic sacrifice.

Carefully read and comprehend the precepts and good lessons of the predecessors, because they are all the crystallization of their life experiences.

The greatest sin of adults is nothing more than staining the pure hearts of children with some dirt.

People should not regard themselves as tall as Mount Tai, but they also do not need to regard themselves as insignificant as a grain of sand.

Taijiquan 188

— Yang Yusheng

There are several ways to practice Taijiquan. In the city, old masters, young masters, ladies, and grandmothers like to play Taijiquan by the mahjong table all day and night! It is said that this kind of "pushing hands" skill, although the "routines" are different, the effect of "nourishing the heart" and "calming the nerves" is the same.

The Taijiquan I am going to talk about now is not like that.

More than ten years ago, I saw many people practicing Taijiquan in Beiping. In the Central Park in the spring and summer seasons, it was simply transformed into a gymnasium, with people practicing everywhere. Among them, there was an old man over seventy years old who practiced the most diligently, and he was seen every morning. Because we saw each other every day, I got to know him and heard him tell me a lot about the benefits of Taijiquan.

According to him, once people pass middle age, if they do not pay attention to health preservation, most of them have excessive fire and weak water, which is extremely harmful to the body. The greatest effect of Taijiquan lies in regulating "water" and "fire" and enriching the inside of the human body. He also said that if you reach the ultimate level of Taijiquan, all "fire" will be eliminated, and you will truly have the style of a "humble gentleman"! There is absolutely no such thing as the bravery and fighting spirit of practicing external martial arts!"

I agree with the point that Taijiquan can regulate "water" and "fire" and enrich the interior. If you say that practicing Taijiquan will eliminate all anger and turn you into a humble gentleman! Then I think it's better not to practice! Because the biggest weakness in the personality of us Chinese is the lack of a considerable amount of "fire"! There are too many people who want to be humble gentlemen! Therefore, there are too few people who can express a spirit of courage and unyielding! How can we withstand practicing Taijiquan again!

Some people say that strengthening the body is one thing, and anger is another. We must first make everyone strong, and then stimulate their proper "anger", so that they can complement each other. Because "strengthening the body" and "anger" are both indispensable things.

I think this sentence may be correct.

The Bloody Tears of a Singing Girl 189

— Jiang Shouqiu

At a banquet of my friend Mr. Zhang, I met a relatively familiar singing girl, who, when the wine was gone and the guests were gone, talked about the pain of the singing girls.

According to her, singing girls originally make a living by their skills, because they are singers, relying on their natural throats; through ordinary research, in a Qingchang teahouse, they use a few tens of yuan in silver to support their families, which, from the standpoint of self-reliance, is also a legitimate profession. However, the general audience who listen to the singing does not care about the quality of the singing, but pays attention to the ugliness; especially those with good faces and loose waistbands are the most popular. If they are well-behaved singing girls, no one is willing to help them, because this kind of audience is not interested in the wine!

Because of this situation, most singing girls have to sacrifice themselves to make their families survive. You must know that in this present time of expensive rice and firewood, relying on only a few packages of silver not only cannot support the family, but even maintaining oneself is not enough. So they have to cater to the needs of the audience and engage in that shameless side business! So the prostitution of singing girls is really forced to this point, and it can also be said to be given by a bad society. You must know that a person always wants to improve, but when it is unavoidable, he has to sacrifice!

After she finished saying these words, her cheeks were covered with tears, and both Mr. Zhang and I felt injustice for them! Really, society treats them too cruelly! Although they want to be singing girls who sell their art but not their bodies, it is impossible in fact! Alas!

It's Difficult to Be a Stand-In 190

— Juan Yin

Xu Zheshen: He is a well-known novelist and essayist of the Shanghai school who is helping to alleviate disaster by lowering his writing fees. In recent years, in addition to writing novels, he has also been writing poetry and essays. This summer, he suddenly suffered a dangerous illness and is now recovering. Therefore, his writing work has been suspended for a long time. A week ago, Xu's poetry and novel correspondence students from all over the country came to Shanghai because of the floods and sought refuge with their teacher to temporarily maintain the status quo. Witnessing the situation, Xu thought of the compatriots of both genders who were suffering in the disaster areas, who must be worse off than the students. Therefore, he vowed to lower his writing fees for three months, and then donate half of the proceeds to help the refugees. People in Shanghai who love Xu's writing can obtain a reduced fee form from 31 Weixin Lane, Xinyuan Sauce Garden Lane, in this city. It not only establishes a literary connection but also benefits the general public.

Little Western Heaven 191

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: Senior Officials Cherish Their Reputation and Have a Knack for Knocking on Doors; New Lovers Leave Their Relatives and Have No Way to Visit the Sick

Looking again, Yueying was actually sitting on the ground, her clothes covered in dust. She was lying on the chair, crying with her shoulders shaking. Even without seeing her face, just hearing her sobbing, one could imagine that she was extremely sad. At this time, sending cosmetics to someone was inevitably a joke. However, the cosmetics were tied up in a large package, which was being held in her hand. In fact, she couldn't throw the things away, and she was so anxious that her face turned red. Jia Duocai was full of grief and anger, and he was hating that there was no way to vent it. Seeing Shi Geng's hesitation, he said: "Shi Lian, just come in and sit, it's nothing. Humph! I have already made a fool of myself." Li Shi hesitantly walked in, blew the dust off the table, and put down the cosmetics. Then he leisurely said to Yueying: "We have a new sister-in-law. Following Old Master Jia, you have risen to the sky in one step. Why are you always crying when things are not good? Moreover, now that you are a wife, you should learn some rules from Old Master Jia. How can you lie on the ground and cry?" Jia Duocai listened to these words, got up immediately, and sighed. Yueying, supporting the chair, stood up and shrank to the corner of the room. She slowly brushed the dust off her body and took out a handkerchief from her body. She rubbed her eyes and then smoothed her hair, saying to Shi Lian: "Mr. Li, how can I not understand what you said? It's not that I insisted on sitting on the ground. I heard that my grandmother is very sick and I want to go back to see her. I begged Old Master Jia last night and I have been begging until now, but Old Master Jia always refuses. Later, I said that if Old Master Jia is really worried, you can go back with me to see her. Fortunately, the road is not far away, just behind this Little Western Heaven." (To be continued)

Royal Incense Drifting Record 192

— Original by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

The Empress Dowager would often raise her hand, carefully examining it with great interest, and sniffing it with her nose, never tiring of it. Not only did she like it herself, but she also wanted to teach us to do the same. However, we could never feel any interest like she did. Only after going to the toilet or getting something fishy or smelly on our hands would we pick some green chrysanthemum leaves to wipe them, in order to offset the dirty smell. At other times, no one was happy to go to the ruined places where those flowers were.

Among the chrysanthemums, it is said that there is also a rare variety called the "Green Peony". Its color is green; definitely not light green, but dark green. There are very few green flowers, and it is not only chrysanthemums that are like this. It seems that green chrysanthemums are particularly rare. I have long heard people say that there is such a thing as a "Green Peony" chrysanthemum, but I have never seen it. The Empress Dowager naturally knew about this different species long ago, so she had been constantly sending people out to search for it for several years. Of course, how could the orders issued by such a towering female politician have no effect at all? Soon, many people offered dozens of pots of chrysanthemums labeled with the words "Green Peony", but the flowers they bloomed only had a slight green color, not enough to be called "green". How could the Empress Dowager be satisfied? So she continued to search. Later, someone sent four pots. At first glance, the color of the flowers was indeed as green as green jade, but after being displayed for a few days, the color suddenly faded. After the Empress Dowager personally examined it carefully, she realized that someone had dyed white chrysanthemums with green color to pretend. Naturally, this made her very angry, and the person who presented the flowers almost fell into the iron window because of this. (426)

The Absurd Points of "Si Lang Visits His Mother" 193

— (Zhang Mengfei)

The play "Si Lang Visits His Mother" is known to be the forte of Tan Xinpei, but after careful examination of the plot, it is not appropriate. When Yang Yanhui married Xiao Bang, which is now Beiping, Tianbo Mansion, where the general lives, was in Tokyo, which is now Henan. The two places are separated by more than a thousand miles, and Si Lang was able to steal the order to leave the customs in one night, see his mother, wife, brothers, nephews, and nieces, and still return to the customs to hand over the order. It went through many twists and turns. Even if there is an airplane to take today, it is beyond reach. I would like to point out this absurdity to your Eminence.

The places visited

Yangzhou Idle Talk 195

— Born in the Jia Chen Year

"Yangzhou Idle Talk" is intended to distinguish it from Yi Junzuo's "Idle Talk about Yangzhou." Moreover, what is written in this article is authentic, genuine Yangzhou idle talk, truly snow tracks and goose tracks from a trip to Yangzhou.

"With a hundred thousand strings of cash around his waist, he rides a crane to Yangzhou," this is the grand gesture of the ancients. Although I, a poor scholar, do not have a hundred thousand strings of cash to spend on travels, my ambition is no less than that of the ancients. Thus, in the early autumn season, I took a steamer down to Yangzhou to visit this place known for its bright moon. I fulfilled a long-cherished wish.

Yangzhou is not only the most important port in Jiangbei, but it has also recently been specially designated by the government as a residential area. Important figures who want to live here are now arriving in droves. The current environment of Yangzhou still retains a simple and unsophisticated charm amidst civilization and enlightenment, making it a truly desirable place to live.

Although the famous scenic spots of Yangzhou cannot be compared with the world-renowned Suzhou and Hangzhou, places such as Slender West Lake, Pingshan Hall, and Green Willow Village are indeed worth lingering over. Moreover, they are purely natural landscapes, with absolutely no artificial intrusions, capturing the spirit of nature. It is this simplicity, tranquility, and elegance that surpasses other places.

The transportation of Yangzhou is extremely smooth, both by water and land. Since the construction of highways throughout Jiangsu Province, it has become even more convenient. Currently, in addition to the Yangzhou-Zhenjiang bus and the connection with the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway train, there are also long-distance buses to Xuzhou and Haizhou in the north, Tianchang in the west, and Nanjing and Wuhu in the south. The inland river steamer routes are especially centered in Yangzhou, with Nanjing, Liuhe, Qingjiang, Gaoyou, Taizhou, Xinghua, and Tongyang routes being numerous. Yangtze River ships sailing up and down the river also stop here. Places like Huojia Bridge and Bajiang Estuary are only about ten miles from the city. If the Jiangsu Construction Department's planned eastern Jiangsu Railway (from the provincial capital to Dongtai) is completed on schedule, the city will become an even more important area.

Daily life in Yangzhou is extremely ordinary. Compared to Suzhou and Shanghai, it is less than half, and compared to the capital, it is only about one-third. A family of eight with an income of twenty or thirty yuan a month can live comfortably and happily without worries. Therefore, there are quite a few civil servants from the capital and provinces who move to Yangzhou to live a retired life. The reason is that renting a house with three rooms only costs two yuan a month in rent. All other daily necessities, such as fish, salt, and vegetables, are reasonably priced. It is no wonder that more and more people are coming from all directions.

The small eateries and restaurants in Yangzhou are particularly inexpensive and of high quality, surpassing any other place. During my short stay of more than ten days in Yangzhou, I ate out almost every meal, and the cost was equivalent to buying groceries myself. If three close friends eat together, it is even cheaper. The Rainbow Building and the China Restaurant outside the Xiaodongmen are particularly unique. Three dishes—stir-fried eel, stir-fried shrimp, and trotters soup—cost only a thousand cash, which is more than enough for four people, and each dish is extremely fresh and delicious.

In the past, Yangzhou flourished due to the gathering of salt merchants, which boosted the market. Now, with the northward relocation of the salt industry to Huaihai, the impact on the area is enormous, and all industries are declining. Currently, with the designation of a residential area and the increasing number of visitors, there is a sense of revival.

Although the development of new businesses in Yangzhou started very early, there has been no success so far. Currently, there are more than ten daily newspapers, but none of them are worth reading. The "New Jiangsu News" and "Su News" from Zhenjiang, the provincial capital, are selling well in the area. Only the "Shen Bao," "Xinwen Bao," and "Shi Bao" from Shanghai can be found. Due to convenient transportation, one can read the newspapers of the day around 5:00 PM every day. It is said that the "Central Daily News" from the capital also arrives daily.
